<div id="review_591887879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/591887879" />
    <a title="Donna ~ The Romance Cover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11672704-donna-the-romance-cover"><img alt="Donna ~ The Romance Cover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369044455p2/11672704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/591887879?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna ~ The Romance Cover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna ~ The Romance Cover" href="/user/show/11672704-donna-the-romance-cover">Donna ~ The Romance Cover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer591887879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10255534740776740677">Leo’s Chance – Mia Sheridan<br/><br/>5 stars!!<br/><br/>Just a reminder that this is Leo (Mia’s first book in this series) told from Leo’s POV, so therefore you need to have read this first for this book to have any meaning. Leo was always going to be a hard act to follow as it was a gorgeous book, but Mia outdid herself with this one. I always thought it would be extremely difficult for a woman to write a man’s POV and some authors have tried and miserably failed, but this author is not one of them.<br/><br/>Just like the f</span>
  <span id="freeText10255534740776740677" style="display:none">Leo’s Chance – Mia Sheridan<br /><br />5 stars!!<br /><br />Just a reminder that this is Leo (Mia’s first book in this series) told from Leo’s POV, so therefore you need to have read this first for this book to have any meaning. Leo was always going to be a hard act to follow as it was a gorgeous book, but Mia outdid herself with this one. I always thought it would be extremely difficult for a woman to write a man’s POV and some authors have tried and miserably failed, but this author is not one of them.<br /><br />Just like the first book, the writing style pulled you in and the writing just flowed and flowed, it is very easy to read. Even though I knew what was going to happen it did not detract from the story as you were seeing it through a totally different perspective. I loved the way that the book went from past to present, it helped a great deal in understanding Leo, I don’t think that anybody truly appreciated what he went through in Leo, but this book brings it all out into the open all the good, bad and the ugly and it could get pretty ugly.<br /><br />Leo had gone through a lot of abuse at the hands of his step mother and he had internalized a lot of the blame for this. He somehow felt that it was his fault and he should harbour some of the guilt because of the way his body had reacted to her. His shrink in the hospital was amazing and such a fab character and I was so glad that he had managed to try and break through Leo’s walls to get him to understand how his step mother had operated. It was also really good to read how he had ensured he did not taint his step fathers memory and had thrown himself 100% into the company as a way of trying to make up for all the wrongs he perceived he had made. I believe deep down he knew that his step father had shouldered a lot of guilt for what happened to Leo and that is probably what ultimately caused his demise.<br /><br />I loved the way that Mia Sheridan managed to make me love Leo even more than I did before. He was always her protector and yet we never truly appreciated the depth of his feelings. The mental torture he puts himself through in this book, trying to weigh up the pros and cons of what he is doing, whether it was fair on Evie what he was doing. Agonising over revealing his true identity, the love he had for her that just oozed out of the pages. I was anxiously awaiting the tattoo reveal and was dreading it, especially knowing what was going to happen…but his torment was crushing…you could tell he truly loved her and it was heart breaking to read. I loved the way we were also shown his agony when he first moved away and the reasons behind him not keeping in touch, it helped to understand so much better.<br /><br />I am a sucker for an epilogue and this book did not disappoint, I was soooo happy, and we got extra scenes. The epilogue was told from Evie’s POV which was a lovely touch. I loved that the steam level in this book was hotter than the first, this really added to the intensity of Leo’s feelings. Reliving the popping of the V was emotional especially when he realised she had saved herself for him. <br /><br />All in all I love this series and this was a brilliant addition and I am so glad that we got to experience this story from both sides of the coin.<br /><br />Loved it!!<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.theromancecover.com">www.theromancecover.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10255534740776740677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/591463824" />
    <a title="Didi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082482-didi"><img alt="Didi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459297426p2/6082482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer591463824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3824031785613415109">IF YOU HAVEN'T READ LEO, DON'T READ LEO'S CHANCE.<br/><br/>IF YOU HAVE READ LEO, THEN YOU'RE IN FOR A TREAT!<br/><br/>Leo's Chance is Leo's story told from his POV. It might seem redundant and although there were definitely areas that were, there was also enough new stuff and revelations added in that prevented boring you out of reading the same book twice.<br/><br/>I LOVED Leo, the book. And the character! But the book is on my fav's of 2013 and therefore reading this was a no-brainer. So despite some repitition I fell in l</span>
  <span id="freeText3824031785613415109" style="display:none">IF YOU HAVEN'T READ LEO, DON'T READ LEO'S CHANCE.<br /><br />IF YOU HAVE READ LEO, THEN YOU'RE IN FOR A TREAT!<br /><br />Leo's Chance is Leo's story told from his POV. It might seem redundant and although there were definitely areas that were, there was also enough new stuff and revelations added in that prevented boring you out of reading the same book twice.<br /><br />I LOVED Leo, the book. And the character! But the book is on my fav's of 2013 and therefore reading this was a no-brainer. So despite some repitition I fell in love with Leo all over again because it was amazing seeing things through his eyes. He is a pained and tortured soul that can't accept he is worthy of love. Seeing him doubt himself and his convictions was heartbreaking. I can't emphasize how much I loved him.<br /><br />The story went between present and past with hospital flashbacks after his car accident. A fateful thing that allowed him to look at his life and re-examine what was once paramount to him. Through the help of his psychologist, Dr. Fox, he comes to truly understand himself and turn a new leaf.<br /><br />Of course the present is where we see Evie again and re-live the beautiful moments that made up the original book and added to the depth of this one. As was the case with Leo, I loved Evie. She was one of those characters that truly deserved the praise others showered her with. You saw that she was kind and considerate, sweet and intelligent, empathetic and forgiving. Sometimes when reading about other heroines I wonder what the hoopla is all about, but not with Evie.<br /><br />The story of Leo and Evie is beautiful and sweet and despite re-visiting the same situations, it was still nice to see Leo's POV and be treated to some new material. The epilogue was beautiful and re-affirmed why I love this couple so much!<br /><br />Beautiful book, wonderful characters, bittersweet, heartfelt story!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3824031785613415109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Its just not plausible. <br/><br/>The other really big criticism I have with this book are the sex scenes - we really dont need that amount of detail Mia Sheridan!!! <br/><br/><a href='http://tinypic.com?ref=25flpqa' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427107ra/853820.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>For example, when Leo is having sex with Evie, he describes every detail right up until he is about to </span>
  <span id="freeText9456396063809308629" style="display:none">Although I liked this book from Leos perspective better than the first book LEO - I still found the story lacking in believability when it comes to Evie not recognising Leo AFTER ONLY EIGHT YEARS !!!!<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=slqxrd" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Sorry, but I cant get over that. Its just not plausible. <br><br>The other really big criticism I have with this book are the sex scenes - we really dont need that amount of detail Mia Sheridan!!! <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=25flpqa" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br>For example, when Leo is having sex with Evie, he describes every detail right up until he is about to orgasm and then tells us how his "balls begin to hitch up......" <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2vimfs0" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>One more thing that drove me mad...<br>Whilst reading the first book Leo, it annoyed the heck out of me how Evie would constantly say "a couple hours" or "a couple things" etc insead of "a couple OF hours" or "a couple OF things" etc etc. I overlooked this as local dialect etc and quirky to the character. HOWEVER, Mia Sheridan used that exact same dialect for Leo in Leos Chance - scuse me but two people - esp two people that have lived in different areas for the last 8 years - just DONT talk exactly the same!!!<br><br>All that said, for all its many flaws, and but for the totally implausible plot, I think Mia Sheridan is a talented writer who shows great promise and with just a bit more experience will be an author well worth watching out for in the future. <br><br><br></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zSgKfAHjMlyxC45qOMT6L6tUdLmWeGaWLYnl9LTizHcD/kg9fAmVpr14498/Upocf7N5e8HTYD1zE1unoA1Mvw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qfnktGKU/Nh1jD7fR2BcC8n0KNUUPrvK49Vm2W+azahnL6b1H35bInn/U2pA9jw4HRMlF0OVvWG9T9iKe3VNYA==')})
  }
//]]>
